The Death of Literary Figure Feng Junmu

Mr. Feng Junmu of Cixi was outstanding in poetry and prose. In recent years, he sold his writings in Shanghai, and seekers came one after another. His body was weak, and he was overworked with thinking. Last winter, his right hand suddenly suffered numbness in three fingers, accompanied by pulling on half of his body. He repeatedly consulted famous Chinese and Western doctors, who concluded that the disease was in the brain and that rescue was not easy. He passed away at 4:00 PM yesterday afternoon. His family has scheduled the encoffining for 1:00 PM today (the 19th).

Page 10

Shanghai Coal Market Already Controlled by the Japanese

Coal Prices Increasing Daily

Chartered Steamers Compete to Transport Coal to Shanghai

Shanghai is a vital transportation hub where various railways converge, with an immense daily demand for fuel coal. Before the suspension of operations, Kailuan coal had the largest share of the market. Since the disruption on the Beining Railway, which prevented Kailuan coal from reaching Shanghai, Japanese coal has swiftly taken the lead in the Shanghai coal market. The surge in imports, rise in coal prices, the rapid escalation, and the current immense influence are truly astonishing. The recent situation is detailed below:

Rapid Increase in Japanese Coal The variety of Japanese coal sold in the Shanghai market is extensive. Popular types include Mitsui, Sakito, Wakamatsu Kazuishi, and Fushun. The most popular of these are Fushun and Mitsui, followed by Sakito. The major distributors in Shanghai are Mitsui, Mitsubishi, and Okabe, among others. Since the suspension of Kailuan coal shipments, Japanese coal has met the demands of the market and various factories and steamships, almost to the point of being unable to meet supply. It has thus leapt to the forefront of the Shanghai fuel coal market. In April of last year, Kailuan coal sales in Shanghai amounted to approximately 120,000 tons, while Fushun coal sales were around 40,000 tons, accounting for one-third. In April of this year, the situation has drastically changed. Due to excessive demand, Fushun coal sales have increased by 81,000 tons compared to the same month last year, making it the leader in coal sales.

British Steamships Switch to Japanese Coal British trading firms in Shanghai, such as Butterfield & Swire (Taikoo) and Jardine Matheson, possess the largest number of steamships and also consume the most coal. Since the suspension of Kailuan coal shipments to Shanghai, British steamships have switched to using Japanese coal to compensate. Taikoo, Jardine Matheson, and other river and ocean steamships have now entered into contracts with Mitsui & Co. to switch to using Mitsui coal. Mitsui coal comes from Mitsui's own coal mines. Taking advantage of the Kailuan disruption, it has secured a huge, long-term customer in the form of British steamships in Shanghai. The company is arranging large-scale shipments.

Chartering Ships for Transportation Over the past two months, businesses in Shanghai dealing in Japanese coal have experienced a surge in business, with daily increases in coal shipments. In addition to their own twenty coal-carrying ships, Mitsui, Mitsubishi, and others have chartered over ten ships from the Dalian Steamship Company to transport coal to Shanghai. They still find that there is too much coal and not enough ships. Mitsui and Dalian Steamship have chartered eight British ships in Shanghai to assist in transporting coal. Furthermore, they have commissioned companies such as R.M. Lambert & Co. to charter over a dozen Chinese merchant ships, including the "Hua Wu" and "Wu Yang," to compete in transporting Japanese coal from Fushun, Mitsui, and Sakito. Due to the high demand and abundant supply, the market price of Japanese coal has gradually increased. The price of Fushun coal has risen several times. Today, the Shanghai coal market is controlled by the Japanese.

Telegram from the Sugar Industry Guild

Regarding the China International Sugar Company

The Shanghai Sugar Industry Guild, noting that Shanghai newspapers have carried advertisements for the China International Sugar Company soliciting distributors for Cuban sugar, yesterday sent a telegram to the Ministry of Industries requesting a thorough investigation and prohibition. It also sent a letter to the China International Sugar Company requesting a detailed response regarding their distribution methods. The telegram and letter are transcribed below:

Telegram to the Ministry of Industries To His Excellency Minister Kong of the Ministry of Industries: This guild has received numerous reports from its members that a Spanish man named Peralta (translated as Po Lai Da) has established the China International Sugar Company on Guangdong Road in Shanghai, claiming to represent the Cuban government and to have signed an agreement with your Ministry to invest US$55.5 million in China to establish sugar factories. Due to a lack of cash, he intends to sell Cuban sugar in China, using the proceeds as the investment capital. He claims that the import of this Cuban sugar has been approved by the Chinese government and is entitled to duty-free import. He also claims that this sugar will soon arrive in China and that to promote sales, it will be priced 25% to 20% lower than Javanese and Japanese sugar. He has also advertised widely for distributors and managers. Sugar is a foodstuff and a necessity for the people's livelihood. In the past, domestic sugar production was substantial, but in recent years it has declined significantly, almost to zero. The reasons for this are twofold: first, domestic manufacturers adhere to outdated methods without making improvements; second, heavy taxes and high costs have allowed foreign sugar to flood the market, with annual imports amounting to over 100 million yuan. Meanwhile, domestic sugar production is languishing, gradually declining. The late President Sun Yat-sen, with his foresight, repeatedly emphasized suppressing foreign goods and revitalizing domestic industries as the key to self-strengthening. Your Excellency, upholding the late President's teachings, is actively promoting domestic industries and sparing no effort. This year's implementation of tax cuts and increased surcharges is intended to revitalize domestic goods. We had hoped that domestic sugar would recover from its decline and that the huge financial drain could be reversed. We were all celebrating and filled with excitement. But unexpectedly, a sudden announcement has been made about the arrival of a large quantity of Cuban sugar in China, which is tantamount to self-destruction, as it will drive domestic sugar into an irreversible state of ruin. Furthermore, we have learned that sugar merchants in our country have been suffering losses due to the impact of high gold and low silver prices. Maintaining the status quo has become extremely difficult. If this large quantity of Cuban sugar is sold at a particularly low price, even if it is only 20% lower, it would still be more than two taels lower than the market price. Shanghai alone has over a million bags of sugar in stock, weighing 1.6 to 1.7 million piculs. The price of this stored sugar would inevitably plummet, resulting in a loss of over 3 million taels in Shanghai alone, not to mention the losses in other ports. The sugar merchants, already deeply wounded, would be unable to withstand this. Few would survive. Therefore, the import of this Cuban sugar would harm merchants and the nation to the utmost. We believe that Your Excellency, who cares for industry and commerce, would not allow this to happen. However, the rumors are persistent, and there must be some basis for them. We, the public, are alarmed, and a sense of impending doom has arisen. The guild is confused and does not know what to do. Therefore, we send this urgent telegram, hoping that Your Excellency will investigate and grant us relief to preserve the last hope for domestic sugar and to sustain the sugar merchants' hard-won businesses. If it is indeed a complete fabrication by this Westerner to deceive and mislead, we hope that Your Excellency will promptly investigate and prohibit it to prevent confusion and ensure the stability of the sugar industry. This is an urgent plea, and we await your instructions. Respectfully, the Shanghai Sugar Industry Guild.

Letter to the China International Sugar Company: We write to you regarding the advertisements placed by your company in the Shanghai newspapers soliciting distributors for Cuban sugar. We extend our congratulations on your new initiative. As your company is also engaged in the sugar trade, it has a close relationship with our guild. We look forward to learning more about your organization, its capital (whether sole proprietorship or joint venture, limited or unlimited liability), the names and nationalities of its shareholders, whether it has been registered, its business objectives, distribution procedures, and when the sugar will arrive. We hope to receive a detailed response within three days of receiving this letter so that we can discuss the matter further. We eagerly await your reply.

Yu Hua Wage Dispute Resolved Through Mediation

The wage dispute at the Yu Hua Silk Weaving Factory on Tangshan Road in Hongkou, which led to a joint strike by workers from three factories, was resolved after the authorities intervened and the workers gradually returned to work while awaiting a resolution. The Social Affairs Bureau mediated several times without success. Yesterday at 9:00 AM, the bureau held a final mediation session. Representatives from the management, Li Zhongxuan, and from the workers, Wei Shouchang and Yu Ande, attended, with Wang Bing of the Social Affairs Bureau presiding. After lengthy discussions, a settlement was reached with the following terms: (1) Wages will be calculated at three cents per foot as determined by the factory. (2) The factory shall not change the interweaved fabrics to pure silk fabrics within this year. (3) Wages for the silk reeling department will be 36 cents per package for 60-count cotton yarn and 30 cents per package for 120-count rayon. (4) If the factory has a surplus at the end of the year, bonuses will be paid according to the practice of the former Jinhua Factory, based on merit.

Citywide Silk Factory Wage Dispute

Social Affairs Bureau Intervenes, Aims for Resolution

Over 61,000 male and female silk reeling workers in the city have demanded the restoration of their original wages. The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau summoned representatives for questioning on the afternoon of the 16th to facilitate mediation. Attending were Yue Xiaorong and Chen Xiupu, representatives of the Fourth District Silk Reeling Workers Union; Yuan Yunlong and Yang Gengdi, representatives of the Sixth District Silk Reeling Workers; and Tao Huachen, representative of the Silk Factories Guild. Guo Yongxi, a staff member of the Social Affairs Bureau, presided, with Wang Zhixin recording. The Fourth District Union representatives stated that, at the representatives' congress on March 13, workers had requested that management restore original wage levels. In the Sixth District, there had been a strike due to wage issues in April. Now, the union, based on the workers' request, argues that silk prices increased in February and March and therefore, they demand restoration of original wages starting from May. The management stated that, based on a market price of US$1.88 per pound and an exchange rate of US$31.50 per US$100 Chinese silver, one dan can only be sold for approximately US$240, equivalent to 720 taels of silver. Silk prices have not increased compared to when the agreement was signed last year, so they cannot restore wages. After lengthy discussions, the workers, in consideration of the factories' business operations, proposed temporarily suspending their original request. However, they demanded that the wages be restored according to the agreement starting from June 1st, regardless of the situation. Afterwards, the chairman announced the end of the questioning.

Dispute Over Dock Dues Collected by Cotton Cloth and Customs Declaration Businesses

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Replies to Social Affairs Bureau

The dispute over dock dues collected by cotton cloth and customs declaration businesses has not yet been resolved. As a result, some cotton cloth cargo shipments from this factory are still effectively suspended. The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau instructed the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to investigate the responsibility in terms of business operations and resolve the matter properly. Yesterday, the Chamber of Commerce replied, saying, "In response to your order to investigate and reply regarding the reasons for the responsibility for collecting and paying dock dues, for your review and approval: This Chamber received your Bureau's order No. 9671 on the 2nd of this month, which stated that the dispute between workers of the Customs Declaration Guild and the Cotton Cloth Guild has been resolved. However, the Bureau ordered that we investigate and properly resolve who should collect and pay the dock dues based on business operations, and submit a reply detailing the handling of the matter for reference. We have dispatched personnel to investigate and offer the following points for your consideration: (1) The cotton cloth business only exchanges goods for money and does not have a definite responsibility to pay dues on behalf of customers. (2) The customs declaration business handles customs declarations on behalf of customers, but whether it is willing to accept the responsibility of paying dues on behalf of customers is also entirely voluntary. (3) The responsibility for paying dock dues, based on the above two points, seems to lie with the customer assistants of the cargo owner. Therefore, to resolve this issue, the customer assistants must first express their responsibility. Otherwise, neither business is responsible, and even if mediation is desired, it would be impossible to proceed. We offer these humble opinions based on our investigation and submit this document for your review and approval, as it would be in the public interest."

Measures for Shops Accepting Deposits

Ministry of Finance Stipulates Modified Method

The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau received an order to handle the case of prohibiting ordinary companies and shops from concurrently operating savings businesses. The Bureau drafted five measures and submitted them to the Municipal Government, which forwarded them to the Ministry of Finance for review and instructions. Details have been repeatedly reported in this newspaper. It is said that the Ministry of Finance originally intended to include the acceptance of deposits by ordinary shops in the prohibition. However, the Bureau believes that very few ordinary shops operate without using their own capital and accepting deposits. A sudden prohibition would have a significant impact on the future of commerce. It proposed to slightly restrict the practice within the bounds of commercial custom. Ordinary shops that do not use the name of savings and follow these measures would be exempt from the prohibition. This was submitted to the Municipal Government and forwarded to the Ministry of Finance for review and reply. The following are two of the modified methods regarding prohibiting shops from accepting deposits: (1) Shops shall not advertise for deposits in newspapers. (2) Shops shall not accept deposits from anyone other than relatives and friends based on mutual trust.

Shop Assistants and Teahouse Staff Not Considered Shop Employees

Interpretation by the Supreme Court

Regarding whether shop apprentices, errand boys, and teahouse staff in hotels, teahouses, and bathhouses should join the trade guild as shop workers or join the labor union as vocational workers, the Supreme Court has interpreted that "Article 8 of the Implementation Rules for Trade Guilds of Industry and Commerce promulgated by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce on January 7, 1930, refers to 'employees.' This was amended and renamed 'shop employees' by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce on January 27, 1931 (Article 10 of the amended rules). 'Shop employees' refers to personnel directly serving in the business operations of the shop. Referring to Article 9 of the amended Implementation Rules for Chambers of Commerce, errand boys and teahouse staff of shops are not considered shop employees. As for shop apprentices, they should be categorized based on whether they directly serve in the business operations."

Leprosy Lecture at the YMCA

Dr. Weeder, a world-renowned leprosy expert, gave a lecture at the YMCA yesterday. Although it was raining heavily, the audience was still very enthusiastic, totaling over 600 people. First, Mr. Wu Zhijian, General Secretary of the Chinese Leprosy Relief Association, gave an introductory speech. Then, Dr. Weeder spoke about the situation at the Culion Leprosarium in the Philippines, translated by Mr. Gao Mingqiang. The main points were that Culion is one of the three islands of Palawan, covering 140 square miles, and is located near many leprosy patients, making it very suitable for establishing a leprosarium. However, there was no treatment in the past, so lepers rarely returned after being exiled. In the past twenty years, more attention has been paid to treatment, and all kinds of facilities have been provided, such as telegraph offices, schools, power plants, police stations, department stores, and prisons, making Culion almost an independent society. Another thing worth mentioning is that in Cebu, the second largest city in the Philippines, there is a leprosy clinic specifically for mild cases to seek treatment. The annual cost is very low, but the results are very significant. This shows that leprosy relief does not require a large amount of funding. Afterwards, a film showing life at the Culion Leprosarium was screened, which was praised by the audience.

Woman with Bound Feet Injured by Tram

Around 5:00 PM the day before yesterday, a trolleybus No. 164 on Route 18, while arriving at the Beinicheng Bridge station, had a passenger Sun Ruiting overzealously ring the bell before other passengers could disembark. The driver, Wang Zhenhai, upon hearing the bell, started the trolley. As the ticket seller Peng Puyayu realized this and rung the bell to stop the trolley, a woman with bound feet by the name of Zhu Wang Shi, 47 years of age and hailing from Haiyan, was getting off the trolley and had her left foot crushed under the left wheel. She fell and was unable to get up. The police investigated the cause of the accident and arrested Sun and sent the injured woman to Baolong Hospital for treatment. However, the injuries were severe, and she died two hours later. The body was taken to the Forensic Center on Feilun Road by the police car for examination. The next morning, the Special District Court was notified, and Prosecutor Guo was commissioned to conduct an examination at the scene. He instructed the woman's son, Zhu Baoquan, to claim the body for burial. Sun Ruiting is suspected of committing a crime and was taken back to the police station to await trial by the court.

Three-Year Runaway Wife Met on a Narrow Road

Wife Escapes with Wit and Words

Husband Refuses to Give Up and Finally Finds Her

Zhang Guifang, a 20-year-old from Huai'an, was betrothed to Wang Jiaxiao, also from the same village, by his parents at a young age. She was immediately taken into his home as a child bride. Not long after, Zhang's father passed away. Because Zhang was young and unable to support himself, he was raised by his uncle, Zhang Jinsheng. Later, due to a famine in their hometown, his uncle brought Zhang and his wife Jiaxiao to Shanghai to learn a trade and make a living. They rented a house at No. 5 Yuncheng Lane, Meixie Road, outside Xiaoximen in Nanshi. By 1928, Jiaxiao had grown into a 19-year-old woman. Zhang's uncle, Jinsheng, sent her to work in a sock factory. Unexpectedly, in June of that year, Jiaxiao seized the opportunity when the family was unprepared and ran away without a trace. Zhang and his uncle searched everywhere, but to no avail. Three years passed, and Zhang had almost forgotten about it. Unexpectedly, they ran into each other on a narrow road near Haichao Temple Street in Xiaonanmen the other day. He immediately forced her to return home. Jiaxiao suddenly claimed that since she ran away, it has been several years. She is now living with her lover, Liu Yuqing, and Liu treats her very badly. Therefore, she deeply regrets it. Even if they had not come looking for her, she had been thinking of returning. However, if she returns with them now, her lover, Liu Yuqing, would feel that he got off too easy. It would be better to wait a while longer, until Liu goes out, and then take all of Liu's belongings and reunite. This should not be late. But this must be kept a secret. Once it is revealed, things will be difficult. Guifang, hearing that his wife had such a passionate heart, deeply believed her. He bid her farewell and they went their separate ways. From then on, Guifang returned home to await good news, hoping for a reunion. Unexpectedly, day after day passed, and not only was there no sign of Jiaxiao, but there was also no news. Only then did he realize that he had been fooled. He started actively investigating again and learned that after his wife had escaped, she and her lover had moved to near the Shanghai Garrison. After finding out the address, he went with his uncle, Jinsheng, to the address around 9:00 PM the other night. They found Jiaxiao, as well as her lover, Liu Yuqing, and brought them both to the Third Sub-station of the First District. After a preliminary interrogation by Director Jin, Liu Yuqing confessed that he was 25 years old, from Hubei, and engaged in the pig slaughtering business. He has known Jiaxiao for many years. They initially lived together in their hometown. Because he was not used to village life, he came to Shanghai for the second time last October. He was recently found by her fiancé. Wang Jiaxiao confessed that she was 22 years old and Guifang was indeed her fiancé. However, his uncle, Jinsheng, was by nature violent. If she disobeyed him, she would be beaten. Therefore, she could not stand the abuse. She then met Liu and ran away to Hubei together. She came to Shanghai last year and has had four children with Liu, two of whom have died. One child is three years old, and she is currently four months pregnant. Director Jin, based on the confessions, immediately drafted a document and sent it to the Shanghai District Court for trial.

One Bandit Shot Dead on Pingliang Road

Around 8:45 PM the other night, a Japanese detective No. 154 from the Yangshupu Road Police Station was patrolling near the intersection of Pingliang Road and Linping Road when he saw a man walking towards him. His movements were suspicious, so he ordered him to stop for inspection. Unexpectedly, the man did not stop and took out a pistol from his sleeve. Seeing the situation was bad, the Japanese detective immediately opened fire, firing a total of twelve shots. The bandit fell to the ground in response. He was taken back to the police station. Upon inspection, he had seven gunshot wounds to the head, chest, and abdomen. The dead bandit was quite large and had a pistol in his hand.

Yesterday's Physician Association Standing Committee Meeting

Local News Two

Bao Fangzhou Arrested

Shanxi Party Department Alleges Bao is a Communist

Claiming He is Actually an Alias of Dong Muchao

Public Security Bureau's Request for Extradition Denied

Result: Released on Bail with a Reputable Shop as Guarantor

The China Mental Research Institute on Bazilu Road, Hongkou, was founded by Bao Fangzhou, a meat sleep scholar. Bao is from Guangdong and studied in Japan in the early years of the Republic of China, specializing in mental science, and has gained considerable experience. He returned to Shanghai after completing his studies in the 7th year of the Republic of China and began to treat people with hypnotism, which was quite effective. He then founded this association. For more than ten years, he has written extensively on mental science, and those who admire his academic ability in the country have established a correspondence department, and they are willing to be listed in the ranks so that it can be widely spread. Therefore, the number of members who have registered to join the Association is increasing day by day, and Bao does not distinguish between gender, so there are many female disciples in particular, such as Ms. Liu Chunyi of Shaanxi, who was elected chairman of the National Assembly held in the capital this time, is also a member, such as Zhang, the vice commander's younger brother Zhang Xueming, the mayor of Tianjin, and the grandson of the late Qing Dynasty State Minister Li, Li Mugong, etc.

All have successively held gifts to ask for advice and Bao's name has become more obvious. Gu This kind of hypnotism, although extremely effective, can only be used for medical treatment, and it is forbidden by all countries in the world to apply it to criminals and interrogate them for confessions. The confessions obtained are after the criminals have lost consciousness, and the criminals are not willing to admit it. It is reported that last year, the highest military authority in this city interrogated a Communist Party member, and the person was unusually cunning. He was repeatedly interrogated and failed to obtain a confession. Bao was once summoned to

Apply the technique to the bandits and get all the secrets, but after the case was finalized, it is not known whether this confession was used as the standard. However, Bao Si always used this matter to flaunt the spirit of his technique, saying that he was deeply praised by the authorities at that time and was happy. Unexpectedly, Bao was suddenly arrested the other day, and his crime was "suspicion of announcing communism," which the world hates. The arrester was the Public Security Bureau of this city. It is said that the Qing Party Committee of the Shanxi Provincial Party Department recently sent a letter stating that Bao Fangzhou, a Cantonese who founded the Mental Research Institute at 176 Bazilu Road, is actually

The alias of the Communist Party member Dong Muchao is using the name of research to promote communism. He should be arrested nearby to curb the chaos. Director Chen Xizeng believed that since the Party Department had reported the accusation, both the false and the real should be thoroughly investigated. Because the address belonged to the Public Concession, Detective Cao Chengqing was sent to Hongkou Police Station the other day to request assistance in the detention. After the head detective obtained a detention warrant from the Special Zone Local Court, he sent Chinese and Western detectives to the address to arrest Bao and immediately searched in detail, only finding the mental

Research Institute membership list, without any books or items involving communism, was sent to the Special Court yesterday morning, and Judge Feng Shide opened the third court for investigation. The Municipal Public Security Bureau did not send a representative to the case, and the Municipal Council was represented by lawyer Li Zhishan, who opposed the extradition of Bao. According to lawyer Li, the police station found that the defendant had been practicing medicine in the concession in the name of Bao Fangzhou for thirteen years, and there was no other name Dong Muchao. The letter from the Shanxi Party Department is difficult to believe. If the Municipal Public Security Bureau wants to request the extradition of the defendant based solely on the letter, then it should

Provide sufficient evidence to prove the facts of the crime, and the police station can agree. The membership list was then submitted to the court. Judge Feng then questioned the defendant, who confessed that his name was Bao Fangzhou, a Cantonese, 38 years old, and his name was not Dong Muchao. There was no Dong Muchao among all the members, which could be carefully examined in the list. He also explained in detail the process of studying hypnotism in Japan and establishing a mental research institute in Shanghai, and that he was summoned by the military authorities of this port last year to test hypnotism.

Asked the bandits for confessions. In detail, he said that he had been in Shanghai for many years, and he was not good at socializing. He had very few friends, and he had never interfered in national affairs. He also asked his lawyer to submit all his works over the years, one by one, requesting them to be checked, so that the defendant's ambition could be judged and he could be released. After consideration, Judge Feng ordered Bao to be released on bail with a reputable shop as guarantor, and waited for the Municipal Public Security Bureau to submit evidence before conducting a further inquiry. It is difficult to predict whether Bao will be extradited or not.

Mad Cow from the Fence

Galloping for Miles, Injuring People and Destroying Property

Western Police Bravely Shot and Killed with Eight Shots

Yesterday morning, a water buffalo suddenly went mad at Fei Xingfa's cattle slaughterhouse at 410 Beijing-Jiang Road, jumped over the wall and escaped, rushing around along the way, injuring many people. It then escaped to the vicinity of Gordon Road in the Public Concession, where it was shot eight times in a row by Western police before falling to the ground dying. The matter was quite interesting, so the beginning and end are recorded as follows:

Roaring and Leaping Out On the morning of yesterday, at about 8:00, Fei Xingfa's cattle slaughterhouse was slaughtering three heads of yellow cattle and one head of water buffalo for customers. Because it was still early, the four cattle were locked in a bamboo fence, ready to be pulled out for slaughter in time. However, at about 10:30, a water buffalo suddenly roared several times, jumped out of the fence, jumped over the wall, and ran wildly in the middle of the road.

Injuring People and Destroying Property The workers in the shop saw the cow jumping over the wall and escaping. Because the water buffalo was strong, they were afraid of causing trouble, so they chased out to capture it, but the cow was like a madman, flying and jumping wildly, hitting with its horns, invincible, and no one dared to resist. The houses in the area of ​​Taiyang Temple Road are all simple, low bungalows. All those who were visited by the cow injured people and destroyed property. Lu Qinghuai, a 12-year-old boy at 16 Longfu Li, Taiyang Temple Road, was the most severely injured. His head was smashed by the cow's horns, and his waist was trampled. Li Zhaodi, an 18-year-old girl on Jingjiang Road, was injured in the legs and arms. Tang Naixing, a straw shed at 49 Taiyang Temple Road, was knocked to the ground, his clothes were torn and bleeding. In particular, the belongings of Xia Dehong's house at 10 Yidexili on the same road were all destroyed, causing considerable losses. (The above-mentioned people have all reported to the Fourth District General Administration). The others who were slightly injured and had furniture damaged are not counted.

Eight Shots to Death Yang Jintang, the chief of the Taiyang Temple Police Station in the Fourth District, learned of this and led the police to pursue it, but the cow was not afraid at all and was as if it were in an uninhabited place. The police officers could do nothing and watched it cross the railway, turn west into Gonghe Road via Datong Road, take Hengfeng Road, cross the Sampan Factory New Bridge, and arrive at Carter Road. At that time, a police officer from the police station saw a water buffalo rushing in like a tide and knew it was a mad cow. He tried to stop it with his hands, but was hit by the cow and fell several feet away, covered in mud. The Western police immediately jumped up and fired eight shots in a row. The cow could no longer support itself and fell to the ground at the intersection of Carter Road and Gordon Road. It was then sent to Longfei Car Company by car. According to the report, the cow ran from Jingjiang Road to Gordon Road, a distance of several miles, crashing into objects, and no one dared to resist it. It was indeed strange that it only fell to the ground and died after being shot eight times.

Pirates Rampant, Kidnapping Two Ship Owners

Extorting 5,000 Yuan Each

To be Redeemed at Dahong Port, North of the Yangtze River

Salt City gang sand ships Lü Changrong, Wang Fashun, etc., loaded with cuttlefish to Song for sale, because of the registration turmoil with the Public Works Bureau Ship Affairs Department, it was delayed for two days. It was not until the other day that the fish was sold out. Each ship agreed to open up and planned to return to the North Ocean to catch the second tide. At about 8:00 on the morning of the former day, eight fish ships of Lü Changrong and others began to sail to Pao Taiwan. Because the wind was not favorable, they stopped and anchored. When the tide came in the evening, they sailed to the Duck Nest Sandy Sea outside the port and suddenly encountered two pirate ships. More than 20 pirates surrounded the fish ships Lü Changlong and Chen Fashun and ordered them to stop. There were five pirates each with a northern accent, each holding a pistol, who jumped on the fish ship with great momentum, and warned them not to make any noise. They locked the crew in a cabin and searched separately. Because there was no silver dollar in the ship, they got nothing, which aroused the anger of the pirates, so they kidnapped the shipowner of Lü Changlong, Lü Taihua, and the shipowner of Chen Fashun, Chen Changfu. Before leaving, they claimed that each person must prepare 5,000 yuan to redeem the tickets at Dahong Port, North of the Yangtze River, otherwise they would be killed. After the pirates left, the two ships returned to Wusong and reported to Baofeng and Cuisheng fish firms, that is, the two firms sent Sun Shaoce (Cuisheng) and Su Zhichun (Baofeng) with the crew to the Fourth District of the Water Police to report the encounter with the pirates and requested the arrest of the pirates and the rescue of the two kidnapped month masters from danger. They also sent warships to protect the export of fish boats and catch the second general purpose. When the two ships were robbed, the other six fish ships of Wang Fashun and others heard the alarm and fled back to Songkou, all daring not to sail. According to the crew of the robbed fish boat, when the pirates were searching, they asked the crew what kind of ships they were. When they answered that they were from the Salt City gang, the pirates asked if they knew Yu Ruoshui in Yancheng. The crew was dumbfounded and could not answer, and the pirates left. Later, according to other boatmen, Yu is a famous pirate leader. The pirates inquired about him, and it is not known what they intended. After receiving the report, the fourth district of the Wusong Water Provincial Public Security Team has ordered the provincial water police Junhe cruiser stationed at the mouth of the Wenzaobang in the Pudong River to quickly sail out of Songkou and track down and suppress the pirates in various oceans.

The Thief Who Throws Bags is Terrible

Do Not Pick Up Anything Left on the Roadside

Otherwise, There Will Be Unexpected Disputes

The methods used by bandits to solicit fraud are different and must be applied according to the person and the location. It is not a one-size-fits-all approach. The bag throwing technique is also a type of solicitation fraud. This technique was very old and seems to be outdated in modern times, but there are still people who are fooled by it, so I will describe the inside story to warn those who are greedy for small profits. When we are walking, if we see one or two yuan or several silver coins abandoned on a remote road, we should not pick them up greedily. Otherwise, someone will suddenly come out to intervene and point out that what we picked up was lost by them. If we do not return it, these people will use this as an excuse to forcibly search and rob us until we have nothing left. There are many such bag throwing bandits in the Hongkou area. The Hongkou police station has successively arrested ten people, including Liu A'san and Yao Bigui, in recent days, and seized four wallets, all of which were used to steal from passers-by using this technique. However, the money in the wallets has been used up. Because the police station needs to investigate the owner, Judge Xiao of the Special Zone Local Court briefly questioned the bandits yesterday and ordered them to be returned to prison for further investigation and punishment.

How Many Jumped into the River

Fortunately, All Were Rescued

A Bowl of Cold Porridge Sparks a Tempest

On the Qinghe Ferry, which travels across the river from the Lan Road Wharf in eastern Shanghai, around 6 PM the night before last, a middle-aged woman suddenly threw herself into the river not far after the ferry departed from the wharf. The ferry captain, Zhang Zhongbing, noticed this and immediately stopped the boat, managing to rescue her. Thankfully, she was saved. She was then sent to the Weituo Wharf Water Police Station. According to the police chief's interrogation, she was a Ms. Zhang Yang, 36 years old, from Funing, Shandong, residing east of the shoe factory on Yangzhou Road. Her husband is named Zhang Beisu, and she has a 17-year-old son named Genkui, who is currently learning a trade elsewhere. She works as a female worker, number 501, at the Shenxin No. 9 Cotton Mill in eastern Shanghai. She stated that at noon today, she saw a bowl of cold porridge that had been left out for several days and smelled bad, so she poured it out. Her husband found out and claimed that times were difficult, and that cold porridge should not be taken lightly, and started to scold her loudly. She scolded back, and her husband raised his hand and beat her fiercely. Neighbors intervened and stopped the fight. Furthermore, her work schedule at the factory happened to be the night shift this week, so she went to bed after eating, waking up at 5 PM to prepare for the night shift. However, her husband continued to make sarcastic remarks, which she could no longer endure. She was consumed with anger and felt that she could no longer tolerate living in such a state, so she decided to seek death. The police chief then sent a detective to bring her husband, Zhang Beisu, to the police station. He confessed that he would not dare to abuse her again and would accept any punishment if he violated this promise. The police chief ordered him to write a statement and take his wife home, treating her kindly.

Unemployment is Dreadful, Youth Despairs of Life

Chen Guozhen, from Suzhou, is 23 years old and resides in Zhabei, Shanghai. He lives with his mother, Ms. Jin. Chen has been unemployed for five years, spending his days at home, sighing in frustration. He has been seeking a suitable position to earn a living, but without success. With the high cost of everything and the high cost of living, making ends meet is difficult. However, Chen continued to strive and fight against his circumstances, hoping to find a way out, but to no avail. Eventually, he became bored and despaired of life. The day before yesterday, around 10 AM, he left home alone, carrying his mother on his back, and went to the Xinguang Wharf. He hired sampan number 1228, stating that he wanted to go to Pudong. When the boat reached the center of the river, he took the opportunity to jump into the river and commit suicide. The boatman, Xin Wenfu, quickly used a bamboo pole to hook him, preventing him from drowning. He was then sent to the Lujiazui Water Police Station. After questioning, Chen revealed the whole story, also stating that the owner of the Zhou Maochang ivory shop in the Xinbei Men area was his friend. The police station immediately sent detective Wu Rongsheng to investigate. That evening, his mother, Ms. Jin, accompanied by a friend, went to the police station to take Chen home.

Gambling is Harmful, Almost Costing a Life

Yesterday morning, around 1 AM, a young man at the Hongkou Nisshin Company Wharf hired sampan number 955 alone, saying he wanted to go to Pudong. When the boat reached the center of the river, he immediately paid the fare of two dimes. In a blink of an eye, he suddenly jumped into the river to commit suicide. Fortunately, the boatman, Yuan Qingting, used a bamboo pole to hook his clothes and rescue him, thus saving his life. Yuan then took him to the Lujiazui Water Police Station for questioning. According to the police chief's interrogation, his name is Chen Jinhe, 24 years old, from Chaozhou. He admitted that he is addicted to gambling and gambles every day. Unfortunately, his luck was bad, and he lost over 200 yuan in just a few days last year. He secretly took the money from the shop, which was discovered by the manager, and he was fired. Since then, he has not found a suitable job. Now, he has run out of money and is struggling to make ends meet. He feels that his future is bleak and hopeless, so he jumped into the river to end his miserable life. The police chief ordered detective Huang Songsheng to investigate and learned that Chen was familiar with the Wanfeng pawnshop on Cais Market Street in the French Concession. He went to the shop to inform them. At 3 AM, his friends Li Jiafen and Liu A'gen went to the police station to take responsibility and escort Chen back, promising to find a way to help him.

At around 2:30 AM the day before yesterday, the body of Tianzi, who was assassinated and shot in the philtrum, was found in front of number 42 Rue Chapsal in the French Concession. After investigation by the Western police, the case was reported to the police station. Detectives were dispatched to move the body to the autopsy room of the Tongren Fuyuan Branch for examination. At the same time last year, the highest was 91.4 degrees, and the lowest was 68.0 degrees.

Special Article

The Bank of China's 1930 Business Report (Continued)

The Decline of the World Market

In 1930, the global economic situation was extremely depressed. Except for France and the Netherlands, almost all governments and people were struggling with economic depression. The most obvious phenomena were: (1) Decline in trade: Trade in all countries decreased compared to the previous year. British imports decreased by 14.4%, and exports decreased by 21%. US imports decreased by 30.4%, and exports decreased by 26.7%. Japanese imports decreased by 30.3%, and exports decreased by 31.6%. German imports (cumulative from January to October) decreased by 24.1% compared to the same period last year, and exports decreased by 8.6%. Even in France, which had the best market conditions, imports increased slightly by 1.1%, but exports inevitably decreased sharply by 14.6%. (2) Increase in the number of unemployed: According to estimates by the International Labor Office, the number of unemployed worldwide reached 11.8 million, double that of the previous year. (3) Decline in prices: Since the European War, the world price index had not changed significantly until 1929. In the spring of 1930, prices suddenly fell sharply. According to the British Board of Trade's survey of wholesale prices, taking the average total in 1924 as 100, food (such as grains, fish, meat, etc.) averaged 87.4 in 1929, but fell to 76.1 in 1930, a drop of 11.3. Non-food items (such as steel, coal, and other minerals, cotton, wool, and other textiles, groceries, etc.) averaged 79.4 in 1929 and 69.6 in 1930, a drop of 9.8. If the total at the end of the year is taken as the standard, the decline is even more severe. The important reasons for the world economic decline are nothing more than the following: (1) Overproduction: During the European War, due to food shortages, producing countries such as Canada, the United States, and Australia vigorously encouraged cultivation and expanded production. Over time, it became impossible to sell the surplus. Manufactured goods also suffered from overproduction due to scientific progress, mass production, and tariff wars. Taking the United States as an example, the inventory of wheat alone reached 10.31 million tons in 1930. Other examples include 1.7 million tons of coffee, 1.35 million tons of cotton, and 280,000 tons of rubber. If the United States, which has the strongest purchasing power, is in this situation, the other countries can be imagined. (2) The artificial manipulation of prices: When prices fall, producers suffer. Therefore, governments often use artificial methods to maintain the prices of goods. For example, the United States and Canada purchase or organize groups to hoard wheat, waiting for a shortage to sell at a higher price. However, with successive bumper harvests, the stockpiles increase, exceeding the capacity of financial resources. As a result, they resort to devaluation and dumping, harming not only wheat producers but also preventing them from selling their products to exchange for other goods. As a result, producers of other goods also fall into a stagnant state. (3) Tariff wars: Overproduction means that one's own country cannot consume enough. Therefore, everyone thinks of using neighboring countries as dumping grounds. At the same time, everyone worries about being used as a dumping ground by neighboring countries. As a result, tariffs are raised, and there is mutual resistance, causing goods to circulate abnormally. The United States, with its wealth surpassing the world and its position as the largest creditor nation, also builds high tariff barriers, leading to the loss of the benefits of international division of labor and causing abnormalities in international trade. Producers often feel insecure because they cannot predict their sales, which can even lead to social instability. In countries that implement protectionist policies, they have no choice but to increase domestic production to compensate for the exclusion of foreign goods, further contributing to the trend of overproduction. (4) Uneven distribution of global gold reserves: As of the end of November 1930, the gold reserves of the 45 countries surveyed worldwide were approximately £2.23 billion. The United States accounted for 38.5%, France accounted for 18%, the United Kingdom accounted for 7%, and the remaining 40 countries accounted for 36.5%, totaling only £800 million. After the European War, global gold reserves were gradually absorbed by the United States and France. The gold reserves of other countries decreased daily. Everyone focused on preserving cash, preventing smooth international finance. Countries that are at a disadvantage in exchange rates constantly pay attention to maintaining and stabilizing the monetary system. For example, Japan's implementation of a tight fiscal policy aimed at concentrating its financial resources on the implementation of the gold standard, which has made the state of industrial and commercial depression even more serious, is clear evidence of this. (5) Other factors, such as excessive speculation in the American business community, creating market panic, the continued decline in silver prices, leading to a reduction in the purchasing power of the Chinese and Indian people, and the political instability in China and India, all directly or indirectly have a negative impact on the world market. There are countless studies, expert writings, and financial institution investigation reports on the above-mentioned topics, so there is no need for us to elaborate further. We will now extract a few points that affect our country and describe them as follows: (1) The main reason for the decline in silver prices lies in the excess of supply over demand. The trend is no different from the general decline in prices. In countries that use gold, silver, as a commodity, although it is still a precious metal, its monetary status has gradually weakened, descending to the ranks of general commodities and having to follow the general price trends. The decline in silver prices in 1930 was of great importance to China's finance and economy, which will be detailed in another chapter. (2) Due to the increasing number of unemployed people in various countries, overseas Chinese were the first to suffer. In the Nanyang area, the number of unemployed overseas Chinese was no less than 400,000. Although there are no detailed statistics on the number of people who returned to China because there were no jobs to be found overseas, it was probably no less than 100,000 in 1930. Compared to the past, when tens of thousands of people went abroad every year, the gain and loss are exactly the opposite. It is estimated that in 1929, the amount of money remitted by overseas Chinese to their home country was approximately 300 million silver dollars, calculated at 15 yuan per pound. In 1930, the pound price reached 20 yuan, but the remittances only amounted to 250 million silver dollars, a decrease of one-sixth in silver and two-fifths in gold. This is extremely detrimental to China's national economy and international exchange rates. (3) Theoretically, China's export trade should increase with the decline in silver prices. However, in 1930, the value of exported goods decreased by 120 million Haikwan taels compared to the previous year. The most significant decrease was in silk, with a decrease of 46 million Haikwan taels. Calculated in gold prices, it was only half of the previous year. More than 80% of silk factories nationwide were closed. The second largest decrease was in agricultural products from the three northeastern provinces. The harvest in 1930 was extremely abundant, but soybean exports decreased by 45 million taels. The market in the three provinces fell sharply as a result, and countless soybean oil businesses went bankrupt. Tea exports decreased by 15 million taels, and leather exports decreased by 11 million taels. On the contrary, the decline in world prices also had some benefits for our country, such as the ability to import wheat and cotton at low prices. The domestic yarn and flour industries were not affected by the shortage of raw materials due to the inland wars, and the rise in gold prices did not significantly threaten the people's clothing and food needs. This is worth mentioning. The following table lists the monthly market prices of rice, wheat, oil, and cotton in 1930, as well as the gold price, for comparison.

Free Talk

Words of Wisdom

— Li Wu

Those who nitpick are our candid friends and should be approached. Those who indulge and forgive are our enemies and should be distanced.

Rather than seeking the favor of a lover with all kinds of deep affection, it is better to show a little filial piety and win the joy of parents.

Love is an stimulant that motivates people to make progress, but also a fatal blow that disheartens them and makes them pessimistic.

Those who give up their seats on trams only want to pity the fair sex, but are unwilling to respect the old and help the young.

Extravagance, luxury, and licentiousness are all factors that contribute to suicide.

There are many lovers who humble themselves and plead for love from beautiful women, but few filial sons who obey their parents and bring joy to their white hair.

Do not envy the success of those who are successful, but emulate their path to success. Do not laugh at the failure of those who have failed, but study the reasons for their failure.

Poverty before being poor can still be reversed. Wealth before being wealthy is ultimately difficult to cure.

People actually abandon every inch of precious time, which is worth a foot of jade, and do not compete for it, only bustling back and forth to compete for trivial profits. Isn't that too foolish?

When moaning on a sickbed, receiving the loving care of a loved one will alleviate the pain, and its effect is far greater than that of any medicine.

Summary of the Sino-Japanese Ancient and Modern Painting Exhibition in Tokyo

— Hua Chan

Japanese painting originated from China. Therefore, ancient Chinese paintings are especially valued. Recently, the government, in order to promote Oriental art and provide opportunities for the people to appreciate it, specially sent Masaki Naohiko and Watanabe Kazan to China to contact collectors and painters in Shanghai, Hangzhou, Suzhou, Beijing, Tianjin, Ping, and Liaoning. Preparations were not completed until the end of the previous month. The venue is the Ueno Park Art Museum in Tokyo. The exhibition period is from April 28 to May 19. On the opening day, President Count Kiyoura Keigo Masaki Naohiko and Honorary President Wang Gunfu, the Chinese Minister, delivered opening speeches. Internal Minister Ichiki Kitokuro, Foreign Minister Shidehara, Education Minister Tanaka, and Chinese representatives Wang Yiting, Liang Hongzhi, Yuan Siyong, etc., all gave congratulatory speeches. Celebrities from all walks of life in Tokyo attended the meeting. The ceremony was extremely grand. The venue was quite magnificent, divided into ancient and modern painting sections. The ancient paintings were mostly works from the Qing Dynasty, followed by the Ming Dynasty, then the Yuan Dynasty. Several Song paintings were also on display. Famous works by Huang Zihjiu, Zhu Derun, and Zhao Danian, collected by the former Qing Dynasty Inner Palace in China, were also on display. Collectors such as Liang Hongzhi, Luo Zhenyu, Zhang Hanqing, Kuai Ruomu, Cao Yuandu, Jin Kaifan, and Luo Yuanjue all had valuable exhibits. It is a pity that collectors from Shanghai and Suzhou did not actively participate, resulting in a significant difference from the original number of pieces. On the Japanese side, however, they collected as much as possible. For example, the Imperial Museum, the Tokyo Art School, and famous collectors in Tokyo and Kyoto all exhibited their fine works, totaling more than 300 pieces, all of which were not seen in the previous exhibition of famous paintings from the Tang, Song, Yuan, and Ming Dynasties. Although there is no doubt that fake works are mixed in, the essence of Chinese painting can also be shown to the world. The modern painting section has more than 200 pieces, collected from Shanghai, Beijing, Tianjin, Hangzhou, Suzhou, etc. The most numerous are from Shanghai, and they are quite exquisite, as the painters are the most prosperous here. Japanese painters have been working hard to improve in recent years. Each person is limited to one piece in this exhibition, and they are all selected carefully crafted, beautiful, and artistically meaningful works to show the characteristics of Japanese painting. Gathering ancient and modern Chinese and foreign paintings in one hall, the advantages and disadvantages are self-evident. I hope Chinese painters will pay more attention to it. The Japanese government and people have always valued art. The enthusiasm of the visitors to this exhibition, the publicity of the media, and the art atmosphere are very strong. Looking back at China, there is no news. Yesterday, I specially visited the painter Ma Mengrong at Rongzhai in Xieqiao and learned about various news from Dongjing. I urgently recorded one or two points to inform those who care about art. Also, the twenty or so painters who went to Japan to participate in the exhibition were warmly welcomed by the Japanese people. They had almost no free days during their trip. It is said that several people will return to Shanghai in late May.

A Record of the Grand Occasion of the Women's Temperance Society Congress

— Sun Choucheng

The Chinese Women's Temperance Association held the opening ceremony of its Second National Congress at Yipinxiang on the 16th of this month. Representatives from ten provinces, including Hunan, Hubei, Guangdong, Guangxi, Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Jiangxi, Anhui, Hebei, Shandong, Jilin, and Liaoning, attended. The scent of perfume and the gleam of hair ornaments filled the hall, making it an unprecedented grand gathering for women in Shanghai. I will record what I saw and heard truthfully, which I believe will also be welcomed by the 200 million female compatriots across the country.

A horizontal banner with the nine characters "When the family is in order, the state is governed, and then the world is at peace" was hung high in the hall. Beside it were couplets that read, "Promote kindness, filial piety, chastity, and frugality" and "Reject tobacco, alcohol, gambling, and vice." On the four walls were posters with slogans such as "Break the decadent polygamous system," "Build a happy monogamous family," "Save the expenses of tobacco, alcohol, gambling, and vice," and "Relieve the suffering of helpless compatriots." Dozens of photographs showcasing the association's various achievements were displayed on both sides, showing scenes of performances, entertainment, and speech contests, all lively and endearing. Portraits of Ms. Willard, the founder of the World Women's Temperance Union, and Ms. Chen Yuling, the pioneer of the temperance movement, were also hung. After signing in, each person was presented with the association's publication, "Temperance," which detailed the drug prevention work and editorial overview of the past ten years. Ms. Yang Meizhen, the chairwoman, wore a small checkered qipao and delivered the opening speech in fluent Mandarin with a composed manner and concise, clear words. Among the representatives, only Madam Zheng Yangxiu and four others wore hair buns. All wore qipaos, with about 30% wearing overcoats and 20% wearing vests over them. In terms of age, those in their twenties were the most numerous, accounting for about 70%. Those under twenty accounted for less than 10%, and those over forty accounted for about 10%. In addition to reporting on the preparatory committee's progress, Liu Wang Liming compared the congress to a furnace, saying that this gathering of opinions from representatives of various provinces, mutual research, was no less than melting various minerals in a furnace to form crystals. She also mentioned that the women's movement in China was still in its infancy, and hoped that the fathers and brothers of the representatives, as well as the male guests present today, would do their best to help. Following this, Mr. Lin Kanghou and Mr. Wang Yunwu successively gave speeches. In addition to agreeing with the Nanjing representatives' four proposals of not hoping to do great things, not talking empty words, focusing on practical work as the goal, not moving people with ideals, and using the most economical methods to do the most work, Mr. Lin also said that the word "temperance" encompasses a great deal. Not only should useless things like tobacco, alcohol, gambling, and vice be tempered, but even beneficial things like reading and exercise should be tempered. Otherwise, overworking the brain or engaging in strenuous exercise can also be dangerous. Mr. Wang said that a recent survey of the habits of prisoners in Shanghai and Hangzhou prisons showed that in Shanghai, 28% smoked opium, 74% smoked cigarettes, 64% drank alcohol, 72% gambled, 32% frequented prostitutes, and 58% were fond of fighting. The habits of prisoners in Hangzhou were less severe than those in Shanghai, which proves that the social environment in Shanghai is worse than in Hangzhou. Your association's goal of rejecting tobacco, alcohol, gambling, and vice carries a major responsibility for transforming society. Today is also the tenth anniversary, and I must come to congratulate you, hoping that your association will develop permanently, tenfold, a hundredfold, a thousandfold, ten thousandfold. Ms. Lin Kecong arrived later, and the chairwoman invited her to speak. Ms. Lin said that although the Civil Code has stipulated equality between men and women, the law is dead. To exercise this women's right, it depends entirely on the educated sisters to come out and educate the uneducated female compatriots. If they still hang yellow cloth sachets on their chests and chant "Amitabha Buddha," I am afraid that even if the law is equal, it will still be of no practical use. Next, Madam Zheng Yangxiu gave a reply speech in Cantonese, saying that "I am an old woman with white hair and I cannot communicate well. I am afraid some people will laugh at my outdated ideas, but I ask myself that although I am an old woman, I can still shoulder social undertakings," and so on. The listeners were moved. After the meeting, there was a banquet. There were many interesting anecdotes told by Yu Rizhang and others at the banquet, but due to space limitations, I will not elaborate.

Xun Huisheng's Three Famous Plays

— Xiuhusheng

When Huisheng came to Shanghai before, the plays he performed for three days were all old plays. The opening night was "Hongluanxi." This time, he performed "Xun Guan Niang," "Xiangluodai," and "Qipan Mountain," which inevitably surprised some people. In fact, all three plays are old scripts that have been renovated. Xun Huisheng's art, his singing is unparalleled in its tenderness, and his acting is divine and transformative. There is nothing that is not excellent, and his expressions are especially wonderfully natural, making it difficult to achieve. He is most able to capture the emotions of the audience, making them unable to control their joy, anger, sorrow, and happiness. Only in this way can he meet the fundamental purpose of an artist and the aesthetic of the people. "Xun Guan Niang" is a highlight play for both women's roles and martial roles. For decades, only Wang Yaoqing has been known for this. Now, Xun Huisheng is the only one who has inherited its true essence. In all four aspects of singing, acting, reciting, and fighting, he is remarkable. This is truly Huisheng's best play. In the past, when Huisheng performed this play, Yaoqing was in the audience watching the play. Some people shouted that he looked very much like Yaoqing, and some people asked if Yaoqing looked like him. Yaoqing also smiled and agreed that it was excellent, which shows how good it is. "Xiangluodai" is a renovated tragic play for young female roles. The scenes are few but very tight. The strangeness of the plot truly makes people wish they could speak out for the injustice of the characters in the play. Among the plays renovated by Huisheng, this should be the most moving. "Qipan Mountain" is a famous play for martial female roles. Huisheng learned it from Yaoqing. Huisheng is the only one who can capture the charming and elegant humor when Dou Xiantong and Xue Dingshan are arranging their marriage. He has also added many humorous and singing interludes to the old script. It is most appropriate for Huisheng to perform it. From this, it can be seen that all three plays are renovated excellent plays of great value. Everywhere, they do not lose Huisheng's original face. It is expected that on the day of the premiere, it will cause a sensation in Shanghai.

A Journey Around the Yellow Sea (7)

— Huang Yanpei

Speaking of immigration, it is originally a major problem in the three northeastern provinces. In the past five or six years, the people of Shandong have been unable to bear the rampant taxation and have voluntarily moved to the eastern provinces. The cumulative total has been nearly two million people, which has greatly irritated the Japanese. In the past two years, because the mainland has been relatively peaceful, people have gradually moved back. When I passed through Dalian, I asked those who handle immigration affairs and learned that this year the number of people who have moved away is not even more than the number of people who have moved back.

Last year, Zhejiang organized a batch of immigrants to Liaoning. The result was very unsatisfactory. It is heard that few remained. The reason is that the management was improper and the preparations were insufficient. Also, the living habits are too different. The people of Zhejiang take rice as their staple food. Once they arrive in the farmland, they cannot find rice. Even if they do, they cannot afford it. Therefore, they feel greatly distressed. Other customs and habits are different in various ways. As a result, they have no choice but to return. More than ten years ago, we also recruited farmers from Jiangsu to cultivate land in the eastern provinces. In the end, there was no good result. We still recruited people from Hebei and Shandong to go. Generally speaking, people with lower levels of knowledge have no way to get spiritual comfort except for material life. Therefore, they rely on material supply more urgently than those with higher levels of knowledge. Therefore, there is a principle for immigration: only people from place A can be moved to place B, and people from place B can be moved to the mainland, but people from place A cannot be moved directly to place C. Japan moves its own people to South Korea, moves South Koreans to North Korea, and moves North Koreans to Liaoji, also for this reason. Recently, it is heard that Hunan is planning to immigrate people to the eastern provinces to solve the famine problem. I wonder if they can avoid repeating the mistakes of Zhejiang.

Speaking of the rice problem above, if this principle is recognized, I think it is better to recruit people from the Yutian and Fengrun areas of Hebei to teach them how to grow it than to recruit people from other places.

Last year, there was also a variety of reasons for the oversupply of soybeans in the eastern provinces. The number of immigrants increased day by day, the cultivated land was expanded day by day, and it happened to be a bumper year. The amount of production increased greatly, and the price of gold was high and the price of silver was low. The European market was not moving, and Japan wanted to use other things to replace bean cakes as fertilizer and was testing it. For these reasons, a phenomenon of supply exceeding demand was created. When I was in the east, I heard that there were still 80,000 cartloads of soybeans and more than 20,000 cartloads of barley in the port of Harbin—each cart is 1,000 poods, and each pood is 30 catties—a certain bank suffered a loss of more than 38 million yuan due to the purchase of soybeans, which could not be compensated. It then issued 60 million Harbin silver notes to cover it up, which shows the seriousness of the impact.

If the government of the eastern provinces thinks that this phenomenon is a temporary coincidence and will not happen again next year, then so be it. Otherwise, a policy should be decided and announced to the people, reducing the planting of soybeans next year and changing to planting something else, so as to avoid being more and more unable to cope next year. This is the responsibility of the government.

Rotary Club

Hawthorne's Detective Case Takes a Turn (16)

— Cheng Xiaoqing

(6) Surprising News

When I went to Hawthorne's residence to reply, it was already half past ten. His servant, Shi Gui, told me that Hawthorne had gone out in the early morning as usual to engage in outdoor exercise and had not yet returned, not even having had breakfast. I secretly pondered Hawthorne's actions. He must also be investigating this person's whereabouts there. However, he has no basis for it. I can't imagine which way he is proceeding. I sat in his office, smoking a cigarette, quietly waiting for him to return. But after eleven o'clock, the cigarettes in the cigarette case had been consumed three times in a row, but Hawthorne still had not returned to his residence. I patiently waited until a quarter past twelve before I saw Hawthorne come in panting from outside. I saw that his face was calm, and he seemed very tired in spirit. It was obvious that his work this morning must have been very intense. He took off his black thin woolen coat and threw himself onto the easy chair. I asked, "Are you running around for last night's business?" Hawthorne just nodded and groped for a cigarette to smoke. I asked again, "Are there any results yet?" Hawthorne shook his head. "That's grinding the back of the knife. I can't say it yet. How are your results?" I told him what had happened. Hawthorne frowned and slowly said, "That's strange. Could it be that my ideals are wrong?" I caught this sentence and hurriedly asked, "What are your ideals? I haven't heard you say it." Hawthorne paused before saying, "According to my guess, this person is neither robbing nor retaliating, but a kind of acid-base reaction caused by misunderstanding." I asked in surprise, "How do you explain this? Could he be with me—" Hawthorne interrupted, "Exactly with you. You have self-knowledge. This matter is of course due to misunderstanding on his part, but you don't need to defend yourself. Last night you were really closer to your little concubine. According to my cold-eyed observation, because of your little concubine's beauty, besides the one who made it difficult for us, there are several young people who seemed to look at you sideways with envy and jealousy. But you are in the game yourself, and you don't feel it." I felt a little uneasy. My ears were slightly hot. I replied, "I also overthought this point. I tried my best to avoid it at the time. It's just that that Peifen is too childish and insisted on sticking to me." Hawthorne said, "Of course I understand this. But in the eyes of others, that unconscious jealousy is also very natural." I said, "In this case, last night's incident was caused by me. But why did he want to play tricks on you?" Hawthorne said, "What's the question? He must also have realized that one person can't beat four hands. Naturally, he had to find a way to divert me first. Therefore, I am satisfied that I may be able to find out the truth about this person from Peifen's mouth. Do you think she would deliberately hide it from you?" I hurriedly replied, "This will never happen. Her temperament and innocent childishness can guarantee her. I dare say that the word 'trickery' has no place in her mind."

Commercial News

Financial Gold Standard Strongly Trending Up

Rumors of Mexico Switching to Gold Coinage

Soaring by Fourteen Taels Outright Yesterday, the gold standard market on the 18th saw a sharp and rapid rise, with only minor fluctuations of around two taels. Throughout the day, there were thirteen or fourteen taels of back and forth movement, ultimately culminating in an astounding surge of fourteen taels. This was truly unbelievable. The pre-market had already exceeded 750 taels, likely due to the decline in the British silver market while foreign exchange rates remained firm, with prices holding steady. Buying sentiment in the market was exceptionally strong, and the post-market was even more aggressive, quickly breaking through the 60-tael barrier. Major players eagerly purchased, and due to the increasingly tight British exchange rates and scarcity of chips, market conditions abruptly shifted to a high point. Industry intentions turned from weak to strong. This morning's large bars are expected to continue falling, it is said.

Breaking the Fifty-Tael Barrier Early This Morning Opening this morning, the July contract added one and a half taels, reaching 749.5 taels. The previous day's large bars reported a low of 1/16, but the silver price did not change. However, private telegrams reported a decline of 1/16, causing some stagnation. There were also rumors of Mexico planning to switch to gold coinage. Subsequently, Yuan Heng, Xin Heng, and others bought in, causing a further rise, totaling 53.67 taels. Foreign exchange tickets were also favorable. In July and August, British Gold Bank initially sold 13.1875, then absorbed 0.1875 until the shilling announcement, when Huabi and others sold 0.1875, and Wanxing Shunli and others also sold, causing it to fall to 51.6 taels. However, the listed price did not change, with only a small reduction of 0.25 for the daily gold and an increase of 0.25 for Hong Kong. Soon, buyers became active, with Yuan Heng, Yuan Mao, Yong Yuan, Cheng Yong, and others entering the market. In addition, the Japanese Commercial Bank offered 1.125 to 1.1875 for July and August British gold, rising to 550,000 at 10:00 AM. Later, Yuan Cheng, Zhi Feng, and Yong others sold, dropping to 53.34 taels at 10:45 AM. Before long, Yuan Xing, Yong Zhi, Feng Yong, Dade Cheng, and Lai entered, immediately adding to 54.4 taels. However, Qian Changxiang and others sold a significant amount. It hit 53 taels at 11:00 AM, then Xin Heng, Tong Taichang, Fu Xing, Cheng Yu, and others entered, and the August British gold only settled at 1.125, rebounding by 2 taels. Since the asphalt market in Hankou re-Jing for 26 taels, it has been increased by 2 qian. Macheng oil is made for 25 taels. The source is still scarce, and the supply is not enough to meet the demand. There is no accumulation in this port. The soap factories that the dealers sold to earlier have not yet settled, and the candle makers are also waiting for the goods. In Zhejiang, the price of Neiping oil has been sold for more than 40 yuan per piece, and there is no goods at the price. Lanolin also needs 35 yuan. This car oil in Jiaxing also wants more than 40 yuan. According to the total, there are less than a thousand pieces, and there is no large vote that can be opened. In short, this year's market has never been seen before. Now it is getting more and more fierce, and it is impossible to estimate the degree to which it can be determined.
